    36	    pub fn minimize_statements(stmts: &mut Vec<'a, Statement<'a>>, ctx: &mut TraverseCtx<'a>) {
    37	        let mut old_stmts = stmts.take_in(ctx.ast);
    38	        let mut is_control_flow_dead = false;
    39	        let mut keep_var = KeepVar::new(ctx.ast);
    40	        for i in 0..old_stmts.len() {
    41	            let stmt = old_stmts[i].take_in(ctx.ast);
    42	            if is_control_flow_dead
    43	                && !stmt.is_module_declaration()
    44	                && !matches!(stmt.as_declaration(), Some(Declaration::FunctionDeclaration(_)))
    45	            {
    46	                keep_var.visit_statement(&stmt);
    47	                continue;
    48	            }
    49	            if Self::minimize_statement(
    50	                stmt,
    51	                i,
    52	                &mut old_stmts,
    53	                stmts,
    54	                &mut is_control_flow_dead,
    55	                ctx,
    56	            )
    57	            .is_break()
    58	            {
    59	                break;
    60	            }
    61	        }
    62	        if let Some(stmt) = keep_var.get_variable_declaration_statement()
    63	            && let Some(stmt) = Self::remove_unused_variable_declaration(stmt, ctx)
    64	        {
    65	            stmts.push(stmt);
    66	        }
    67	
    68	        // Drop a trailing unconditional jump statement if applicable
    69	        if let Some(last_stmt) = stmts.last() {
    70	            match last_stmt {
    71	                // "while (x) { y(); continue; }" => "while (x) { y(); }"
    72	                Statement::ContinueStatement(s) if s.label.is_none() => {
    73	                    let mut changed = false;
    74	                    if let Some(
    75	                        Ancestor::ForStatementBody(_)
    76	                        | Ancestor::ForInStatementBody(_)
    77	                        | Ancestor::ForOfStatementBody(_),
    78	                    ) = ctx.ancestors().nth(1)
    79	                    {
    80	                        stmts.pop();
    81	                        changed = true;
    82	                    }
    83	                    if changed {
    84	                        ctx.state.changed = true;
    85	                    }
    86	                }
    87	                // "function f() { x(); return; }" => "function f() { x(); }"
    88	                Statement::ReturnStatement(s) if s.argument.is_none() => {
    89	                    if let Ancestor::FunctionBodyStatements(_) = ctx.parent() {
    90	                        stmts.pop();
    91	                        ctx.state.changed = true;
    92	                    }
    93	                }
    94	                _ => {}
    95	            }
    96	        }
    97	
    98	        // Merge certain statements in reverse order
    99	        if stmts.len() >= 2 && ctx.options().sequences {
   100	            if let Some(Statement::ReturnStatement(_)) = stmts.last() {
   101	                'return_loop: while stmts.len() >= 2 {
   102	                    let prev_index = stmts.len() - 2;
   103	                    let prev_stmt = &stmts[prev_index];
   104	                    match prev_stmt {
   105	                        Statement::ExpressionStatement(_) => {
   106	                            if let Some(Statement::ReturnStatement(last_return)) = stmts.last()
   107	                                && last_return.argument.is_none()
   108	                            {
   109	                                break 'return_loop;
   110	                            }
   111	                            ctx.state.changed = true;
   112	                            // "a(); return b;" => "return a(), b;"
   113	                            let last_stmt = stmts.pop().unwrap();
   114	                            let Statement::ReturnStatement(mut last_return) = last_stmt else {
   115	                                unreachable!()
   116	                            };
   117	                            let prev_stmt = stmts.pop().unwrap();
   118	                            let Statement::ExpressionStatement(mut expr_stmt) = prev_stmt else {
   119	                                unreachable!()
   120	                            };
   121	                            let b = last_return.argument.as_mut().unwrap();
   122	                            let argument = Self::join_sequence(&mut expr_stmt.expression, b, ctx);
   123	                            let right_span = last_return.span;
   124	                            let last_return_stmt =
   125	                                ctx.ast.statement_return(right_span, Some(argument));
   126	                            stmts.push(last_return_stmt);
   127	                        }
   128	                        // Merge the last two statements
   129	                        Statement::IfStatement(if_stmt) => {
   130	                            // The previous statement must be an if statement with no else clause
   131	                            if if_stmt.alternate.is_some() {
   132	                                break 'return_loop;
   133	                            }
   134	                            // The then clause must be a return
   135	                            let Statement::ReturnStatement(_) = &if_stmt.consequent else {
   136	                                break 'return_loop;
   137	                            };
   138	
   139	                            ctx.state.changed = true;
   140	                            let last_stmt = stmts.pop().unwrap();
   141	                            let Statement::ReturnStatement(last_return) = last_stmt else {
   142	                                unreachable!()
   143	                            };
   144	                            let prev_stmt = stmts.pop().unwrap();
   145	                            let Statement::IfStatement(prev_if) = prev_stmt else { unreachable!() };
   146	                            let mut prev_if = prev_if.unbox();
   147	                            let Statement::ReturnStatement(prev_return) = prev_if.consequent else {
   148	                                unreachable!()
   149	                            };
   150	
   151	                            let left_span = prev_return.span;
   152	                            let right_span = last_return.span;
   153	                            // "if (a) return; return b;" => "return a ? void 0 : b;"
   154	                            let mut left = prev_return
   155	                                .unbox()
   156	                                .argument
   157	                                .unwrap_or_else(|| ctx.ast.void_0(left_span));
   158	                            // "if (a) return a; return;" => "return a ? b : void 0;"
   159	                            let mut right = last_return
   160	                                .unbox()
   161	                                .argument
   162	                                .unwrap_or_else(|| ctx.ast.void_0(right_span));
   163	
   164	                            // "if (!a) return b; return c;" => "return a ? c : b;"
   165	                            if let Expression::UnaryExpression(unary_expr) = &mut prev_if.test
   166	                                && unary_expr.operator.is_not()
   167	                            {
   168	                                prev_if.test = unary_expr.argument.take_in(ctx.ast);
   169	                                std::mem::swap(&mut left, &mut right);
   170	                            }
   171	
   172	                            let argument = if let Expression::SequenceExpression(sequence_expr) =
   173	                                &mut prev_if.test
   174	                            {
   175	                                // "if (a, b) return c; return d;" => "return a, b ? c : d;"
   176	                                let test = sequence_expr.expressions.pop().unwrap();
   177	                                let mut b = Self::minimize_conditional(
   178	                                    prev_if.span,
   179	                                    test,
   180	                                    left,
   181	                                    right,
   182	                                    ctx,
   183	                                );
   184	                                Self::join_sequence(&mut prev_if.test, &mut b, ctx)
   185	                            } else {
   186	                                // "if (a) return b; return c;" => "return a ? b : c;"
   187	                                Self::minimize_conditional(
   188	                                    prev_if.span,
   189	                                    prev_if.test.take_in(ctx.ast),
   190	                                    left,
   191	                                    right,
   192	                                    ctx,
   193	                                )
   194	                            };
   195	                            let last_return_stmt =
   196	                                ctx.ast.statement_return(right_span, Some(argument));
   197	                            stmts.push(last_return_stmt);
   198	                        }
   199	                        _ => break 'return_loop,
   200	                    }
   201	                }
   202	            } else if let Some(Statement::ThrowStatement(_)) = stmts.last() {
   203	                'throw_loop: while stmts.len() >= 2 {
   204	                    let prev_index = stmts.len() - 2;
   205	                    let prev_stmt = &stmts[prev_index];
   206	                    match prev_stmt {
   207	                        Statement::ExpressionStatement(_) => {
   208	                            ctx.state.changed = true;
   209	                            // "a(); throw b;" => "throw a(), b;"
   210	                            let last_stmt = stmts.pop().unwrap();
   211	                            let Statement::ThrowStatement(mut last_throw) = last_stmt else {
   212	                                unreachable!()
   213	                            };
   214	                            let prev_stmt = stmts.pop().unwrap();
   215	                            let Statement::ExpressionStatement(mut expr_stmt) = prev_stmt else {
   216	                                unreachable!()
   217	                            };
   218	                            let argument = Self::join_sequence(
   219	                                &mut expr_stmt.expression,
   220	                                &mut last_throw.argument,
   221	                                ctx,
   222	                            );
   223	                            let right_span = last_throw.span;
   224	                            let last_throw_stmt = ctx.ast.statement_throw(right_span, argument);
   225	                            stmts.push(last_throw_stmt);
   226	                        }
   227	                        // Merge the last two statements
   228	                        Statement::IfStatement(if_stmt) => {
   229	                            // The previous statement must be an if statement with no else clause
   230	                            if if_stmt.alternate.is_some() {
   231	                                break 'throw_loop;
   232	                            }
   233	                            // The then clause must be a throw
   234	                            let Statement::ThrowStatement(_) = &if_stmt.consequent else {
   235	                                break 'throw_loop;
   236	                            };
   237	
   238	                            ctx.state.changed = true;
   239	                            let last_stmt = stmts.pop().unwrap();
   240	                            let Statement::ThrowStatement(last_throw) = last_stmt else {
   241	                                unreachable!()
   242	                            };
   243	                            let prev_stmt = stmts.pop().unwrap();
   244	                            let Statement::IfStatement(prev_if) = prev_stmt else { unreachable!() };
   245	                            let mut prev_if = prev_if.unbox();
   246	                            let Statement::ThrowStatement(prev_throw) = prev_if.consequent else {
   247	                                unreachable!()
   248	                            };
   249	
   250	                            let right_span = last_throw.span;
   251	                            let mut left = prev_throw.unbox().argument;
   252	                            let mut right = last_throw.unbox().argument;
   253	
   254	                            // "if (!a) throw b; throw c;" => "throw a ? c : b;"
   255	                            if let Expression::UnaryExpression(unary_expr) = &mut prev_if.test
   256	                                && unary_expr.operator.is_not()
   257	                            {
   258	                                prev_if.test = unary_expr.argument.take_in(ctx.ast);
   259	                                std::mem::swap(&mut left, &mut right);
   260	                            }
   261	
   262	                            let argument = if let Expression::SequenceExpression(sequence_expr) =
   263	                                &mut prev_if.test
   264	                            {
   265	                                // "if (a, b) throw c; throw d;" => "throw a, b ? c : d;"
   266	                                let test = sequence_expr.expressions.pop().unwrap();
   267	                                let mut b = Self::minimize_conditional(
   268	                                    prev_if.span,
   269	                                    test,
   270	                                    left,
   271	                                    right,
   272	                                    ctx,
   273	                                );
   274	                                Self::join_sequence(&mut prev_if.test, &mut b, ctx)
   275	                            } else {
   276	                                // "if (a) throw b; throw c;" => "throw a ? b : c;"
   277	                                Self::minimize_conditional(
   278	                                    prev_if.span,
   279	                                    prev_if.test.take_in(ctx.ast),
   280	                                    left,
   281	                                    right,
   282	                                    ctx,
   283	                                )
   284	                            };
   285	                            let last_throw_stmt = ctx.ast.statement_throw(right_span, argument);
   286	                            stmts.push(last_throw_stmt);
   287	                        }
   288	                        _ => break 'throw_loop,
   289	                    }
   290	                }
   291	            }
   292	        }
   293	    }
   294	
   295	    fn minimize_statement(
   296	        stmt: Statement<'a>,
   297	        i: usize,
   298	        stmts: &mut Vec<'a, Statement<'a>>,
   299	        result: &mut Vec<'a, Statement<'a>>,
   300	        is_control_flow_dead: &mut bool,
   301	
   302	        ctx: &mut TraverseCtx<'a>,
   303	    ) -> ControlFlow<()> {
   304	        match stmt {
   305	            Statement::EmptyStatement(_) => (),
   306	            Statement::BreakStatement(s) => {
   307	                *is_control_flow_dead = true;
   308	                result.push(Statement::BreakStatement(s));
   309	            }
   310	            Statement::ContinueStatement(s) => {
   311	                *is_control_flow_dead = true;
   312	                result.push(Statement::ContinueStatement(s));
   313	            }
   314	            Statement::VariableDeclaration(var_decl) => {
   315	                Self::handle_variable_declaration(var_decl, result, ctx);
   316	            }
   317	            Statement::ExpressionStatement(expr_stmt) => {
   318	                Self::handle_expression_statement(expr_stmt, result, ctx);
   319	            }
   320	            Statement::SwitchStatement(switch_stmt) => {
   321	                Self::handle_switch_statement(switch_stmt, result, ctx);
   322	            }
   323	            Statement::IfStatement(if_stmt) => {
   324	                if Self::handle_if_statement(i, stmts, if_stmt, result, ctx).is_break() {
   325	                    return ControlFlow::Break(());
   326	                }
   327	            }
   328	            Statement::ReturnStatement(ret_stmt) => {
   329	                Self::handle_return_statement(r<response clipped><NOTE>To save on context only part of this file has been shown to you.    383	    fn handle_variable_declaration(
   384	        mut var_decl: Box<'a, VariableDeclaration<'a>>,
   385	        result: &mut Vec<'a, Statement<'a>>,
   386	
   387	        ctx: &mut TraverseCtx<'a>,
   388	    ) {
   389	        if let Some(first_decl) = var_decl.declarations.first_mut()
   390	            && let Some(first_decl_init) = first_decl.init.as_mut()
   391	        {
   392	            let changed = Self::substitute_single_use_symbol_in_statement(
   393	                first_decl_init,
   394	                result,
   395	                ctx,
   396	                false,
   397	            );
   398	            if changed {
   399	                ctx.state.changed = true;
   400	            }
   401	        }
   402	        if Self::substitute_single_use_symbol_within_declaration(
   403	            var_decl.kind,
   404	            &mut var_decl.declarations,
   405	            ctx,
   406	        ) {
   407	            ctx.state.changed = true;
   408	        }
   409	
   410	        // If `join_vars` is off, but there are unused declarators ... just join them to make our code simpler.
   411	        if !ctx.options().join_vars
   412	            && var_decl.declarations.iter().all(|d| !Self::should_remove_unused_declarator(d, ctx))
   413	        {
   414	            result.push(Statement::VariableDeclaration(var_decl));
   415	            return;
   416	        }
   417	
   418	        if let Some(Statement::VariableDeclaration(prev_var_decl)) = result.last()
   419	            && var_decl.kind == prev_var_decl.kind
   420	        {
   421	            ctx.state.changed = true;
   422	        }
   423	        let VariableDeclaration { span, kind, declarations, declare, .. } = var_decl.unbox();
   424	        for mut decl in declarations {
   425	            if Self::should_remove_unused_declarator(&decl, ctx) {
   426	                ctx.state.changed = true;
   427	                if let Some(init) = decl.init.take()
   428	                    && init.may_have_side_effects(ctx)
   429	                {
   430	                    result.push(ctx.ast.statement_expression(init.span(), init));
   431	                }
   432	            } else {
   433	                if let Some(Statement::VariableDeclaration(prev_var_decl)) = result.last_mut()
   434	                    && kind == prev_var_decl.kind
   435	                {
   436	                    prev_var_decl.declarations.push(decl);
   437	                    continue;
   438	                }
   439	                let decls = ctx.ast.vec1(decl);
   440	                let new_decl = ctx.ast.alloc_variable_declaration(span, kind, decls, declare);
   441	                result.push(Statement::VariableDeclaration(new_decl));
   442	            }
   443	        }
   444	    }
   445	
   446	    fn handle_expression_statement(
   447	        mut expr_stmt: Box<'a, ExpressionStatement<'a>>,
   448	        result: &mut Vec<'a, Statement<'a>>,
   449	
   450	        ctx: &mut TraverseCtx<'a>,
   451	    ) {
   452	        let changed = Self::substitute_single_use_symbol_in_statement(
   453	            &mut expr_stmt.expression,
   454	            result,
   455	            ctx,
   456	            false,
   457	        );
   458	        if changed {
   459	            ctx.state.changed = true;
   460	        }
   461	
   462	        if ctx.options().sequences
   463	            && let Some(Statement::ExpressionStatement(prev_expr_stmt)) = result.last_mut()
   464	        {
   465	            let a = &mut prev_expr_stmt.expression;
   466	            let b = &mut expr_stmt.expression;
   467	            expr_stmt.expression = Self::join_sequence(a, b, ctx);
   468	            result.pop();
   469	            ctx.state.changed = true;
   470	        }
   471	        // "var a; a = b();" => "var a = b();"
   472	        match &mut expr_stmt.expression {
   473	            Expression::AssignmentExpression(assign_expr) => {
   474	                let merged = Self::merge_assignment_to_declaration(assign_expr, result, ctx);
   475	                if merged {
   476	                    ctx.state.changed = true;
   477	                    return;
   478	                }
   479	            }
   480	            Expression::SequenceExpression(sequence_expr) => {
   481	                if result
   482	                    .last()
   483	                    .is_some_and(|stmt| matches!(stmt, Statement::VariableDeclaration(_)))
   484	                {
   485	                    let first_non_merged_index =
   486	                        sequence_expr.expressions.iter_mut().position(|expr| {
   487	                            if let Expression::AssignmentExpression(assign_expr) = expr {
   488	                                !Self::merge_assignment_to_declaration(assign_expr, result, ctx)
   489	                            } else {
   490	                                true
   491	                            }
   492	                        });
   493	                    let sequence_len = sequence_expr.expressions.len();
   494	                    match first_non_merged_index {
   495	                        None => {
   496	                            // all elements are merged
   497	                            ctx.state.changed = true;
   498	                            return;
   499	                        }
   500	                        Some(val) if val == sequence_len - 1 => {
   501	                            // all elements are merged except for the last expression
   502	                            let last_expr = sequence_expr.expressions.pop().unwrap();
   503	                            result.push(ctx.ast.statement_expression(last_expr.span(), last_expr));
   504	                            ctx.state.changed = true;
   505	                            return;
   506	                        }
   507	                        Some(0) => {
   508	                            // no elements are merged
   509	                        }
   510	                        Some(val) => {
   511	                            sequence_expr.expressions.drain(0..val);
   512	                            ctx.state.changed = true;
   513	                        }
   514	                    }
   515	                }
   516	            }
   517	            _ => {}
   518	        }
   519	
   520	        result.push(Statement::ExpressionStatement(expr_stmt));
   521	    }
   522	
   523	    fn merge_assignment_to_declaration(
   524	        assign_expr: &mut AssignmentExpression<'a>,
   525	        result: &mut Vec<'a, Statement<'a>>,
   526	        ctx: &TraverseCtx<'a>,
   527	    ) -> bool {
   528	        if assign_expr.operator != AssignmentOperator::Assign {
   529	            return false;
   530	        }
   531	        let AssignmentTarget::AssignmentTargetIdentifier(id) = &assign_expr.left else {
   532	            return false;
   533	        };
   534	        let Some(Statement::VariableDeclaration(var_decl)) = result.last_mut() else {
   535	            return false;
   536	        };
   537	        if !matches!(&var_decl.kind, VariableDeclarationKind::Var | VariableDeclarationKind::Let) {
   538	            return false;
   539	        }
   540	        for decl in var_decl.declarations.iter_mut().rev() {
   541	            let BindingPattern::BindingIdentifier(kind) = &decl.id else {
   542	                break;
   543	            };
   544	            if kind.name == id.name {
   545	                if decl.init.is_none()
   546	                    && (decl.kind == VariableDeclarationKind::Var
   547	                        || assign_expr.right.is_literal_value(true, ctx))
   548	                {
   549	                    // "var a; a = b();" => "var a = b();"
   550	                    decl.init = Some(assign_expr.right.take_in(ctx.ast));
   551	                    return true;
   552	                }
   553	                // Note it is not possible to compress like:
   554	                // - "var a = b(); a = c();" => "var a = (b(), c());"
   555	                //   This is not possible as we need to consider cases when `c()` accesses `a`
   556	                // - "var a = 1; a = b();" => "var a = b();"
   557	                //   This is not possible as we need to consider cases when `b()` accesses `a`
   558	                // - "let a; a = foo(a);" => "let a = foo(a);"
   559	                //   This is not possible as TDZ error would be introduced
   560	                break;
   561	            }
   562	            // should not move assignment above variables with initializer to keep the execution order
   563	            if decl.init.is_some() {
   564	                break;
   565	            }
   566	            // should not move assignment above other variables for let
   567	            // this could cause TDZ errors (e.g. `let a, b; b = a;`)
   568	            if decl.kind == VariableDeclarationKind::Let {
   569	                break;
   570	            }
   571	        }
   572	        false
   573	    }
   574	
   575	    fn handle_switch_statement(
   576	        mut switch_stmt: Box<'a, SwitchStatement<'a>>,
   577	        result: &mut Vec<'a, Statement<'a>>,
   578	
   579	        ctx: &mut TraverseCtx<'a>,
   580	    ) {
   581	        let changed = Self::substitute_single_use_symbol_in_statement(
   582	            &mut switch_stmt.discriminant,
   583	            result,
   584	            ctx,
   585	            false,
   586	        );
   587	        if changed {
   588	            ctx.state.changed = true;
   589	        }
   590	
   591	        if ctx.options().sequences
   592	            && let Some(Statement::ExpressionStatement(prev_expr_stmt)) = result.last_mut()
   593	        {
   594	            let a = &mut prev_expr_stmt.expression;
   595	            let b = &mut switch_stmt.discriminant;
   596	            switch_stmt.discriminant = Self::join_sequence(a, b, ctx);
   597	            result.pop();
   598	            ctx.state.changed = true;
   599	        }

  1240	    fn substitute_single_use_symbol_in_expression_from_declarators(

  1290	    /// Returns Some(true) when the expression is successfully replaced.
  1291	    /// Returns Some(false) when the expression is not replaced, and cannot try the subsequent expressions.
  1292	    /// Return None when the expression is not replaced, and can try the subsequent expressions.
  1293	    ///
  1294	    /// `substituteSingleUseSymbolInExpr`: <https://github.com/evanw/esbuild/blob/v0.25.9/internal/js_parser/js_parser.go#L9642>
  1295	    fn substitute_single_use_symbol_in_expression(
  1296	        target_expr: &mut Expression<'a>,
  1297	        search_for: &str,
  1298	        replacement: &mut Expression<'a>,
  1299	        replacement_has_side_effect: bool,
  1300	        ctx: &TraverseCtx<'a>,
  1301	    ) -> Option<bool> {
  1302	        match target_expr {
  1303	            Expression::Identifier(id) => {
  1304	                if id.name == search_for {
  1305	                    *target_expr = replacement.take_in(ctx.ast);
  1306	                    return Some(true);
  1307	                }
  1308	                // If the identifier is not a getter and the identifier is read-only,
  1309	                // we know that the value is same even if we reordered the expression.
  1310	                if let Some(symbol_id) = ctx.scoping().get_reference(id.reference_id()).symbol_id()
  1311	                    && !ctx.scoping().symbol_is_mutated(symbol_id)
  1312	                {
  1313	                    return None;
  1314	                }
  1315	            }
  1316	            Expression::AwaitExpression(await_expr) => {
  1317	                if let Some(changed) = Self::substitute_single_use_symbol_in_expression(
  1318	                    &mut await_expr.argument,
  1319	                    search_for,
  1320	                    replacement,
  1321	                    replacement_has_side_effect,
  1322	                    ctx,
  1323	                ) {
  1324	                    return Some(changed);
  1325	                }
  1326	            }
  1327	            Expression::YieldExpression(yield_expr) => {
  1328	                if let Some(argument) = &mut yield_expr.argument
  1329	                    && let Some(changed) = Self::substitute_single_use_symbol_in_expression(
  1330	                        argument,
  1331	                        search_for,
  1332	                        replacement,
  1333	                        replacement_has_side_effect,
  1334	                        ctx,
  1335	                    )
  1336	                {
  1337	                    return Some(changed);
  1338	                }
  1339	            }
  1340	            Expression::ImportExpression(import_expr) => {
  1341	                if let Some(changed) = Self::substitute_single_use_symbol_in_expression(
  1342	                    &mut import_expr.source,
  1343	                    search_for,
  1344	                    replacement,
  1345	                    replacement_has_side_effect,
  1346	                    ctx,
  1347	                ) {
  1348	                    return Some(changed);
  1349	                }
  1350	
  1351	                // The "import()" expression has side effects but the side effects are
  1352	                // always asynchronous so there is no way for the side effects to modify
  1353	                // the replacement value. So it's ok to reorder the replacement value
  1354	                // past the "import()" expression assuming everything else checks out.
  1355	                if !replacement_has_side_effect && !import_expr.source.may_have_side_effects(ctx) {
  1356	                    return None;
  1357	                }
  1358	            }
  1359	            Expression::UnaryExpression(unary_expr) => {
  1360	                if unary_expr.operator != UnaryOperator::Delete
  1361	                    && let Some(changed) = Self::substitute_single_use_symbol_in_expression(
  1362	                        &mut unary_expr.argument,
  1363	                        search_for,
  1364	                        replacement,
  1365	                        replacement_has_side_effect,
  1366	                        ctx,
  1367	                    )
  1368	                {
  1369	                    return Some(changed);
  1370	                }
  1371	            }
  1372	            Expression::StaticMemberExpression(member_expr) => {
  1373	                if let Some(changed) = Self::substitute_single_use_symbol_in_expression(
  1374	                    &mut member_expr.object,
  1375	                    search_for,
  1376	                    replacement,
  1377	                    replacement_has_side_effect,
  1378	                    ctx,
  1379	                ) {
  1380	                    return Some(changed);
  1381	                }
  1382	            }
  1383	            Expression::BinaryExpression(binary_expr) => {
  1384	                if let Some(changed) = Self::substitute_single_use_symbol_in_expression(
  1385	                    &mut binary_expr.left,
  1386	                    search_for,
  1387	                    replacement,
  1388	                    replacement_has_side_effect,
  1389	                    ctx,
  1390	                ) {
  1391	                    return Some(changed);
  1392	                }
  1393	                if let Some(changed) = Self::substitute_single_use_symbol_in_expression(
  1394	                    &mut binary_expr.right,
  1395	                    search_for,
  1396	                    replacement,
  1397	                    replacement_has_side_effect,
  1398	                    ctx,
  1399	                ) {
  1400	                    return Some(changed);
  1401	                }
  1402	            }
  1403	            Expression::AssignmentExpression(assign_expr) => {
  1404	                if assign_expr.left.may_have_side_effects(ctx) {
  1405	                    // Do not reorder past a side effect in an assignment target, as that may
  1406	                    // change the replacement value. For example, "fn()" may change "a" here:
  1407	                    // ```js
  1408	                    // let a = 1;
  1409	                    // foo[fn()] = a;
  1410	                    // ```
  1411	                    return Some(false);
  1412	                }
  1413	                if assign_expr.operator != AssignmentOperator::Assign && replacement_has_side_effect
  1414	                {
  1415	                    // If this is a read-modify-write assignment and the replacement has side
  1416	                    // effects, don't reorder it past the assignment target. The assignment
  1417	                    // target is being read so it may be changed by the side effect. For
  1418	                    // example, "fn()" may change "foo" here:
  1419	                    // ```js
  1420	                    // let a = fn();
  1421	                    // foo += a;
  1422	                    // ```
  1423	                    return Some(false);
  1424	                }
  1425	                if replacement_has_side_effect {
  1426	                    // If the assignment target may depend on side effects of the replacement,
  1427	                    // don't reorder it past the assignment target. The non-last part of the
  1428	                    // assignment target is evaluated before the assignment evaluation so that
  1429	                    // part may be changed by the side effect. For example, "fn()" may change
  1430	                    // "foo" here:
  1431	                    // ```js
  1432	                    // let a = fn();
  1433	                    // foo.bar = a;
  1434	                    // ```
  1435	                    let may_depend_on_side_effect = match &assign_expr.left {
  1436	                        AssignmentTarget::AssignmentTargetIdentifier(_) => false,
  1437	                        AssignmentTarget::ComputedMemberExpression(member_expr) => {
  1438	                            Self::is_expression_that_reference_may_change(&member_expr.object, ctx)
  1439	                        }
  1440	                        AssignmentTarget::PrivateFieldExpression(member_expr) => {
  1441	                            Self::is_expression_that_reference_may_change(&member_expr.object, ctx)
  1442	                        }
  1443	                        AssignmentTarget::StaticMemberExpression(member_expr) => {
  1444	                            Self::is_expression_that_reference_may_change(&member_expr.object, ctx)
  1445	                        }
  1446	                        AssignmentTarget::ArrayAssignmentTarget(_)
  1447	                        | AssignmentTarget::ObjectAssignmentTarget(_)
  1448	                        | AssignmentTarget::TSAsExpression(_)
  1449	                        | AssignmentTarget::TSNonNullExpression(_)
  1450	                        | AssignmentTarget::TSSatisfiesExpression(_)

  1500	                ) {
  1501	                    return Some(changed);
  1502	                }
  1503	            }
  1504	            Expression::ConditionalExpression(cond_expr) => {
  1505	                if let Some(changed) = Self::substitute_single_use_symbol_in_expression(
  1506	                    &mut cond_expr.test,
  1507	                    search_for,
  1508	                    replacement,
  1509	                    replacement_has_side_effect,
  1510	                    ctx,
  1511	                ) {
  1512	                    return Some(changed);
  1513	                }
  1514	                // Do not substitute our unconditionally-executed value into a branch
  1515	                // unless the value itself has no side effects
  1516	                if !replacement_has_side_effect {
  1517	                    // Unlike other branches in this function such as "a && b" or "a?.[b]",
  1518	                    // the "a ? b : c" form has potential code evaluation along both control
  1519	                    // flow paths. Handle this by allowing substitution into either branch.
  1520	                    // Side effects in one branch should not prevent the substitution into
  1521	                    // the other branch.
  1522	
  1523	                    let consequent_changed = Self::substitute_single_use_symbol_in_expression(
  1524	                        &mut cond_expr.consequent,
  1525	                        search_for,
  1526	                        replacement,
  1527	                        replacement_has_side_effect,
  1528	                        ctx,
  1529	                    );
  1530	                    if consequent_changed == Some(true) {
  1531	                        return consequent_changed;
  1532	                    }
  1533	                    let alternate_changed = Self::substitute_single_use_symbol_in_expression(
  1534	                        &mut cond_expr.alternate,
  1535	                        search_for,
  1536	                        replacement,
  1537	                        replacement_has_side_effect,
  1538	                        ctx,
  1539	                    );
  1540	                    if alternate_changed == Some(true) {
  1541	                        return alternate_changed;
  1542	                    }
  1543	                    // Side effects in either branch should stop us from continuing to try to
  1544	                    // substitute the replacement after the control flow branches merge again.
  1545	                    if consequent_changed == Some(false) || alternate_changed == Some(false) {
  1546	                        return Some(false);
  1547	                    }
  1548	                }
  1549	            }
  1550	            Expression::ComputedMemberExpression(member_expr) => {
  1551	                if let Some(changed) = Self::substitute_single_use_symbol_in_expression(

  1553	                    search_for,
  1554	                    replacement,
  1555	                    replacement_has_side_effect,
  1556	                    ctx,
  1557	                ) {
  1558	                    return Some(changed);
  1559	                }
  1560	                // Do not substitute our unconditionally-executed value into a branch
  1561	                // unless the value itself has no side effects
  1562	                if (!replacement_has_side_effect || !member_expr.optional)
  1563	                    && let Some(changed) = Self::substitute_single_use_symbol_in_expression(

  1565	                        search_for,

  1567	                        replacement_has_side_effect,
  1568	                        ctx,
  1569	                    )
  1570	                {
  1571	                    return Some(changed);
  1572	                }
  1573	            }
  1574	            Expression::PrivateFieldExpression(private_field_expr) => {
  1575	                if let Some(changed) = Self::substitute_single_use_symbol_in_expression(

2026-05-31 10:38:25,192 - INFO - swea-agent-oxc-project__oxc-20810 - 💭 THOUGHT
Now I can see the issue! In `substitute_single_use_symbol_in_expression`, when handling `ObjectExpression`, it only matches on `PropertyKey::StaticIdentifier(_)` and `PropertyKey::PrivateIdentifier(_)` - but it does NOT handle `PropertyKey::StringLiteral(_)` or `PropertyKey::NumericLiteral(_)` etc. When a property key is a string literal like `"test-a"` (which cannot be represented as a static identifier because of the hyphen), the function falls into the `match_expression!(PropertyKey)` branch, which calls `Self::substitute_single_use_symbol_in_expression` on the key, and then returns `Some(false)`.

This means if a property with a string literal key (like `"test-a"`) comes BEFORE the property that we want to inline the variable into (like `testb: o`), the function stops early and returns `Some(false)`, preventing the substitution of the variable into the later property.

Let me verify this understanding. The issue: when we have:
```ts
var o = "test-b", l = {
    "test-a": "test-a",
    testb: o,
};
```

The function tries to inline `o` into the object. It iterates over properties:
1. First property: `"test-a": "test-a"` - key is `PropertyKey::StringLiteral`. The match falls into the catch-all `match_expression!(PropertyKey)` branch. It checks the key for the variable, doesn't find it, but then returns `Some(false)` which prevents looking at subsequent properties.
2. Second property: never reached.

The fix should be: when the property key is a string literal that doesn't need to be computed (i.e., it's a string literal that is already a valid property key), we should continue to the value substitution instead of stopping with `Some(false)`.

Let me look at the code more carefully:

```rust
Expression::ObjectExpression(obj_expr) => {
    for prop in &mut obj_expr.properties {
        match prop {
            ObjectPropertyKind::ObjectProperty(prop) => match prop.key {
                PropertyKey::StaticIdentifier(_)
                | PropertyKey::PrivateIdentifier(_) => {
                    // ... substitute in prop.value
                    return Some(changed);
                }
                match_expression!(PropertyKey) => {
                    // try substitute in key expression
                    // ...
                    // Stop now because computed keys have side effects
                    return Some(false);
                }
            },
```

The problem is that `PropertyKey::StringLiteral` and `PropertyKey::NumericLiteral` are not `StaticIdentifier` or `PrivateIdentifier`, so they fall into the catch-all `match_expression!(PropertyKey)` branch. But string literals and numeric literals are not computed keys that have side effects - they are literal keys. The code should handle them similarly to `StaticIdentifier`.

Let me check what `match_expression!(PropertyKey)` covers:

So `PropertyKey` has:
- `StaticIdentifier`
- `PrivateIdentifier`
- And inherits from `Expression` (which includes `StringLiteral`, `NumericLiteral`, `Identifier`, etc.)

The issue is clear now. In the `substitute_single_use_symbol_in_expression` function, when processing an `ObjectExpression`, it matches on `ObjectPropertyKind::ObjectProperty(prop)` and then matches on `prop.key`:

1. `PropertyKey::StaticIdentifier(_)` - handled correctly
2. `PropertyKey::PrivateIdentifier(_)` - handled correctly  
3. Everything else (via `match_expression!(PropertyKey)`) - this includes `StringLiteral`, `NumericLiteral`, and other expression-based keys.

For string literal keys like `"test-a"` that are computed property keys (i.e., `prop.computed` is `true`), the key expression itself might have side effects. But for non-computed string literal keys like `"test-a"` in `{ "test-a": "test-a" }`, the key is just a literal and has no side effects. The code currently treats ALL expression-based keys as potential side-effect sources and returns `Some(false)`.

However, looking more carefully, I see that `StringLiteral` keys like `"test-a"` where `prop.computed` is `false` are actually safe to continue past. The issue is that the code doesn't distinguish between computed and non-computed expression-based keys.

Wait, let me re-examine. In the object literal `{ "test-a": "test-a", testb: o }`:
- `"test-a"` is a `PropertyKey` which is `StringLiteral` (inherited from `Expression`)
- `testb` is a `PropertyKey` which is `StaticIdentifier`

The code matches `PropertyKey::StaticIdentifier` for `testb` and tries to substitute in `prop.value`. But for `"test-a"`, it falls into the catch-all and returns `Some(false)` prematurely.

The fix should be: for non-computed property keys that are literals (like `StringLiteral`, `NumericLiteral`, `BooleanLiteral`), we should handle them similarly to `StaticIdentifier` - just try to substitute in `prop.value` and then continue, rather than stopping.

use std::path::PathBuf;

#[test]
fn test_inline_variable_with_string_key() {
    let source = r#"var o = "test-b", l = {
    "test-a": "test-a",
    testb: o,
};
export { l };"#;
    
    let expected = r#"var l = {
    "test-a": "test-a",
    testb: "test-b"
};
export { l };"#;
    
    // Use the minifier
    let allocator = oxc_allocator::Allocator::default();
    let source_type = oxc_span::SourceType::mjs();
    let mut program = oxc_parser::Parser::new(&allocator, source, source_type).parse_program().unwrap();
    
    let options = oxc_minifier::CompressOptions::default();
    oxc_minifier::Compressor::new(&allocator).build(&mut program, options);
    
    let result = oxc_codegen::Codegen::new().build(&program).source_text;
    
    assert_eq!(result, expected, "Expected:\n{}\n\nGot:\n{}", expected, result);
}
EOF

    90	    let allocator = Allocator::default();
    91	    let ret = Parser::new(&allocator, source_text, source_type)
    92	        .with_options(ParseOptions { allow_return_outside_function: true, ..Default::default() })
    93	        .parse();
    94	    assert!(!ret.panicked, "{source_text}");
    95	    assert!(ret.errors.is_empty(), "{source_text}");

    97	    if let Some(options) = options {
    98	        Compressor::new(&allocator).build(&mut program, options);
    99	    }
   100	    Codegen::new()

   103	        .code

// Save as inline test in the existing test file

use oxc_minifier::{CompressOptions, CompressOptionsKeepNames};
use oxc_span::SourceType;

use crate::{default_options, test, test_options, test_options_source_type, test_same};

#[test]
fn test_repro_string_key_before_variable_inline() {
    // This should inline `o` but currently doesn't when string key "test-a" comes first
    test(
        r#"var o = "test-b", l = { "test-a": "test-a", testb: o }; export { l };"#,
        r#"var l = { "test-a": "test-a", testb: "test-b" }; export { l };"#,
    );
    
    // This works correctly when quotes can be removed
    test(
        r#"var o = "test-b", l = { testa: "test-a", testb: o }; export { l };"#,
        r#"var l = { testa: "test-a", testb: "test-b" }; export { l };"#,
    );
}
ENDOFFILE

2026-05-31 10:45:16,481 - INFO - swea-agent-oxc-project__oxc-20810 - 💭 THOUGHT
The test fails as expected. The variable `o` is not being inlined because the string key `"test-a"` comes before `testb: o`. Now let me fix the issue.

The problem is in `substitute_single_use_symbol_in_expression` function in `minimize_statements.rs`. When processing `ObjectExpression`, the code handles `PropertyKey::StaticIdentifier` and `PropertyKey::PrivateIdentifier` but falls through to the catch-all for `StringLiteral` and `NumericLiteral` keys, which then returns `Some(false)` prematurely.

The fix: we need to handle literal keys (StringLiteral, NumericLiteral, BooleanLiteral, etc.) similarly to StaticIdentifier - just try to substitute in the property value and continue. The key distinction is whether the key is computed (has side effects) or not.

Let me look at the code more carefully:

```rust
Expression::ObjectExpression(obj_expr) => {
    for prop in &mut obj_expr.properties {
        match prop {
            ObjectPropertyKind::ObjectProperty(prop) => match prop.key {
                PropertyKey::StaticIdentifier(_)
                | PropertyKey::PrivateIdentifier(_) => {
                    // try substitute in prop.value
                    return Some(changed);
                }
                match_expression!(PropertyKey) => {
                    // try substitute in key expression
                    // ...
                    // Stop now because computed keys have side effects
                    return Some(false);
                }
            },
```

Actually, I need to understand the logic better. The comment says "Stop now because computed keys have side effects". But not all expression-based keys are computed - `StringLiteral` and `NumericLiteral` keys can be non-computed. The `prop.computed` field tells us whether the key is computed.

For non-computed properties with string/numeric literal keys, the key has no side effects and we should be able to continue past it to substitute in later properties. For computed properties, we should still stop.

Actually, looking at it more carefully: the issue isn't about whether the key has side effects. The function is trying to find the variable `o` and replace it with its value. When it encounters a string literal key like `"test-a"`, it should just skip over it and continue looking at subsequent properties, because the string literal key doesn't contain the variable `o` (it's a literal). The only reason to stop would be if the key has side effects that could affect the variable.

So the fix is: for non-computed property keys that are simple literals (StringLiteral, NumericLiteral, BooleanLiteral, etc.), we should treat them like StaticIdentifier - just try to substitute in the value and continue if not found.

But wait, there's another subtlety. Let me re-read the code flow:

1. It iterates through properties
2. For each property, it tries to find and replace the variable in the key and value
3. If it finds the variable in the value (`return Some(changed)`), it stops
4. If it doesn't find it, it returns `Some(false)` for computed keys (meaning "can't continue past this")
5. For StaticIdentifier, if not found in value, it returns whatever the substitution returned (which could be `None` meaning "continue to next property")

The issue is that for `StringLiteral` keys, the code falls into the `match_expression!(PropertyKey)` branch and always returns `Some(false)`. But for non-computed `StringLiteral` keys, the key is just a literal with no side effects, so we should be able to continue.

Let me look at the `match_expression!(PropertyKey)` branch:

```rust
match_expression!(PropertyKey) => {
    if let Some(changed) =
        Self::substitute_single_use_symbol_in_expression(
            prop.key.to_expression_mut(),
            search_for,
            replacement,
            replacement_has_side_effect,
            ctx,
        )
    {
        return Some(changed);
    }
    // Stop now because computed keys have side effects
    return Some(false);
}
```

The comment says "Stop now because computed keys have side effects" - but the check for whether the key is actually computed is missing! We should only return `Some(false)` if the key is actually computed (i.e., `prop.computed` is true). For non-computed expression keys (like `"test-a"`), we should continue to the next property by returning `None`.

Wait, but we also need to try substituting in the value. Let me think about this...

For a property like `{ "test-a": "test-a" }`:
- Key is `StringLiteral("test-a")`, not computed
- Value is `StringLiteral("test-a")`
- We should try to substitute in the value, and if not found, continue to next property

For a property like `{ [x]: y }`:
- Key is `Identifier("x")`, computed
- Value is `Identifier("y")`
- We should try to substitute in the key, then the value, then stop if not found (because computed keys have side effects)

So the fix should be: when the property key is an expression but NOT computed (i.e., `prop.computed` is false), we should handle it like `StaticIdentifier` - try to substitute in `prop.value` and then continue.

Let me look at how to check if the key is computed. The `ObjectProperty` has a `computed` field:

Good, `ObjectProperty` has a `computed` field. Now let me fix the code.

The current code in `minimize_statements.rs` lines 1720-1779:

```rust
Expression::ObjectExpression(obj_expr) => {
    for prop in &mut obj_expr.properties {
        match prop {
            ObjectPropertyKind::ObjectProperty(prop) => match prop.key {
                PropertyKey::StaticIdentifier(_)
                | PropertyKey::PrivateIdentifier(_) => {
                    if let Some(changed) =
                        Self::substitute_single_use_symbol_in_expression(
                            &mut prop.value,
                            search_for,
                            replacement,
                            replacement_has_side_effect,
                            ctx,
                        )
                    {
                        if prop.shorthand && prop.key.is_specific_id("__proto__") {
                            // { __proto__ } -> { ['__proto__']: value }
                            prop.computed = true;
                            prop.key =
                                PropertyKey::from(ctx.ast.expression_string_literal(
                                    prop.key.span(),
                                    "__proto__",
                                    None,
                                ));
                        }
                        prop.shorthand = false;
                        return Some(changed);
                    }
                }
                match_expression!(PropertyKey) => {
                    if let Some(changed) =
                        Self::substitute_single_use_symbol_in_expression(
                            prop.key.to_expression_mut(),
                            search_for,
                            replacement,
                            replacement_has_side_effect,
                            ctx,
                        )
                    {
                        return Some(changed);
                    }
                    // Stop now because computed keys have side effects
                    return Some(false);
                }
            },
            ObjectPropertyKind::SpreadProperty(prop) => {
                // ...
            }
        }
    }
}
```

The fix should be: when the property key is an expression variant but `prop.computed` is `false`, we should handle it like `StaticIdentifier` - just try to substitute in the value and continue.

But wait, there's another issue: the match branch `PropertyKey::StaticIdentifier(_) | PropertyKey::PrivateIdentifier(_)` returns the result of substitution, but for the expression variants, we need to return `None` (not `Some(false)`) to continue to the next property when the substitution isn't found.

Wait, I need to reconsider. The original code for `StaticIdentifier` and `PrivateIdentifier` didn't have a `continue` - it would just fall through. Let me check what the original behavior was for when substitution fails on a `StaticIdentifier` key:

Looking at the original code, when we have `PropertyKey::StaticIdentifier(_) | PropertyKey::PrivateIdentifier(_)` and the substitution in `prop.value` returns `None` (meaning not found but can continue), the match arm doesn't have an explicit `return`, so it falls through to the end of the `for` loop and continues to the next property. That's correct.

But with my change, for non-computed properties, I explicitly `continue` after failing to find the variable in the value. That should be equivalent.

However, I also need to think about what happens if `prop.computed` is `true` but the key is `StaticIdentifier` or `PrivateIdentifier`. That seems like a contradiction - `StaticIdentifier` and `PrivateIdentifier` are never computed. But just in case, the original code handled them together regardless of `computed`. My new code puts them in the `else` branch (when `prop.computed` is true). Let me check: can `StaticIdentifier` or `PrivateIdentifier` ever have `computed = true`?

Looking at the parser, `{ [a]: 1 }` would produce a computed property with key being an `Expression::Identifier`, not `PropertyKey::StaticIdentifier`. So `StaticIdentifier` and `PrivateIdentifier` should never have `computed = true`. But just to be safe, I should keep the original handling for those.

Actually wait, my refactored code is wrong. If `prop.computed` is `false`, we handle it in the first branch. But if `prop.computed` is `true` and the key is `StaticIdentifier` or `PrivateIdentifier`, we go to the second branch which also tries to substitute in the value. But this situation should never happen.

But there's a bigger issue: for `prop.computed = false` with `match_expression!(PropertyKey)` keys (like `StringLiteral`), the original code would try to substitute in the key first (via `prop.key.to_expression_mut()`), then the value. My new code only tries the value. But for non-computed expression keys like `StringLiteral`, the key is a literal and can't contain the variable we're looking for, so it's fine to skip it.

use oxc_allocator::Allocator;
use oxc_codegen::{Codegen, CodegenOptions};
use oxc_minifier::{CompressOptions, Compressor};
use oxc_parser::Parser;
use oxc_span::SourceType;

fn run(source_text: &str) -> String {
    let allocator = Allocator::default();
    let source_type = SourceType::mjs();
    let ret = Parser::new(&allocator, source_text, source_type).parse();
    assert!(ret.errors.is_empty(), "{source_text}");
    let mut program = ret.program;
    Compressor::new(&allocator).build(&mut program, CompressOptions::smallest());
    Codegen::new()
        .with_options(CodegenOptions { single_quote: true, ..Default::default() })
        .build(&program)
        .code
}

fn main() {
    // Test case from PR description - should inline variable
    let input1 = r#"var o = "test-b", l = { "test-a": "test-a", testb: o }; export { l };"#;
    println!("Input:  {}", input1);
    println!("Output: {}", run(input1));
    println!();
    
    // Test case that already works - no string key with hyphens
    let input2 = r#"var o = "test-b", l = { testa: "test-a", testb: o }; export { l };"#;
    println!("Input:  {}", input2);
    println!("Output: {}", run(input2));
}
ENDOFFILE

2026-05-31 10:48:51,782 - INFO - swea-agent-oxc-project__oxc-20810 - 💭 THOUGHT
Let me just run the existing test to confirm the fix works as expected. But first, let me think about edge cases.

**Edge cases to consider:**

1. **Multiple string literal keys before the target variable:**
   ```ts
   var o = "test-b", l = { "a": "1", "b": "2", testb: o };
   ```
   Should still inline `o`.

2. **Computed keys with side effects should still stop:**
   ```ts
   var o = "test-b", l = { [sideEffect()]: "1", testb: o };
   ```
   Should NOT inline `o` past the computed key (because it has side effects).

3. **Numeric literal keys:**
   ```ts
   var o = "test-b", l = { 1: "one", testb: o };
   ```
   Should inline `o`.

4. **Boolean literal keys (though unusual):**
   ```ts
   var o = "test-b", l = { true: "yes", testb: o };
   ```
   Should inline `o`.

5. **String literal key that contains the variable name:**
   ```ts
   var o = "test-b", l = { "o": o, testb: o };
   ```
   The string `"o"` is a literal, not a reference to variable `o`. The value `o` should be inlined.

6. **Multiple properties with string keys, variable used in a later one:**
   ```ts
   var o = "test-b", l = { "test-a": "test-a", "test-c": "test-c", testb: o };
   ```
   Should inline.

Let me verify case 2 (computed keys with side effects) separately - the current code for computed keys should still work correctly since we only changed the non-computed path.

Let me verify by looking at the code flow again. My change is:
1. If `!prop.computed`: try to substitute in value, if found return `Some(changed)`, else `continue` to next property.
2. If `prop.computed`: same as original logic - try key then value, return `Some(false)` if not found.

This looks correct. But wait, I need to double-check: what about `StaticIdentifier` and `PrivateIdentifier` keys? They are never computed. In the original code, they were in the first branch which didn't check `computed`. In my new code, I moved them to the `else` branch (when `prop.computed` is true). But since `StaticIdentifier` and `PrivateIdentifier` are never computed, they would always be handled by the `if !prop.computed` branch. That's fine.

But wait, there's a subtle issue. The original code tried to substitute in `prop.key.to_expression_mut()` for expression-based keys (like `StringLiteral`). My new code skips that for non-computed keys and only tries the value. That should be fine because for non-computed expression keys like `StringLiteral`, the key is a literal and can't contain a variable reference.

However, what if the property key is an expression that could contain the variable? For example:
```ts
var o = "test-b", l = { [o]: "test", testb: o };
```
Here `[o]` is a computed property with key being the variable `o`. This has `computed = true`, so it goes to the else branch and is handled correctly.

What about:
```ts
var o = "test-b", l = { o: "test", testb: o };
```
Here `o` is a `StaticIdentifier` key (shorthand might be true). This has `computed = false`, so it goes to the first branch and tries to substitute in `prop.value`. The key `o` is a static identifier, not the variable `o` (they're different things). So it should continue past it. That's correct.

Now let me think about whether there's a case where a non-computed expression key could contain the variable we're trying to inline. I don't think so - non-computed keys are always literals or static identifiers. They can't contain variable references.

Let me also think about the `__proto__` shorthand handling. In the original code, when we found the variable in the value and the key was `__proto__` with shorthand, it would convert it to `['__proto__']: value`. In my new code, I kept this logic in both branches. But wait, `__proto__` as a shorthand would be a `StaticIdentifier` key with `shorthand = true`. Since `StaticIdentifier` is not computed, it goes to the first branch. The `__proto__` handling is there. Good.

Actually, I realize my code might have a problem with the `__proto__` check. In the original code, `prop.key.is_specific_id("__proto__")` was checked. But in my new code, the `__proto__` handling is in the `if !prop.computed` branch, which is correct because `__proto__` as a shorthand is always a `StaticIdentifier` with `computed = false`.

But wait, there's another issue: the original code also had `prop.key.is_specific_id("__proto__")` in the `StaticIdentifier`/`PrivateIdentifier` branch. In my new code, I moved `StaticIdentifier`/`PrivateIdentifier` to the `else` branch (computed keys). But `StaticIdentifier` can never be computed. So the `__proto__` check in the `else` branch would never be reached. That's fine - the `__proto__` check in the first branch handles it.

Hmm, actually let me reconsider the structure. Let me re-examine:

The original code had:
```rust
match prop.key {
    PropertyKey::StaticIdentifier(_) | PropertyKey::PrivateIdentifier(_) => {
        // try value, handle __proto__, return Some(changed)
    }
    match_expression!(PropertyKey) => {
        // try key, return Some(changed) or Some(false)
    }
}
```

My new code has:
```rust
if !prop.computed {
    // try value, handle __proto__, return Some(changed)
    // continue to next property
} else {
    match &mut prop.key {
        PropertyKey::StaticIdentifier(_) | PropertyKey::PrivateIdentifier(_) => {
            // try value, handle __proto__, return Some(changed)
        }
        match_expression!(PropertyKey) => {
            // try key, return Some(changed) or Some(false)
        }
    }
}
```

For `StaticIdentifier`/`PrivateIdentifier` keys (which are never computed), the original code would try the value and then if not found, fall through (no return) and continue to the next property. My new code does the same: `continue` to the next property.

For expression keys that are NOT computed (like `"test-a"` string literal), the original code would try the key first, then return `Some(false)` if not found. My new code skips the key (since it's a literal) and tries the value, then continues if not found. This is the fix.

For expression keys that ARE computed (like `[x]`), my new code goes to the else branch and behaves like the original: try the key, return `Some(changed)` or `Some(false)`.

This all looks correct.

But I should also think about: what if the non-computed key is an expression that IS the variable we're looking for? For example:
```ts
var o = "test-b", l = { o: "test", testb: o };
```
Here `o` in the key position is a `StaticIdentifier`, not an expression reference to the variable `o`. It's an identifier name, not a variable reference. So this case is handled correctly.

What about:
```ts
var o = "test-b", l = { "o": "test", testb: o };
```
Here `"o"` is a string literal key. It's not a reference to variable `o`. So skipping the key and going to the value is correct.

I'm confident the fix is correct. Let me also check that the test suite still passes fully (we already verified).

Now let me think about whether there are any other similar patterns in the codebase that might have the same issue. Let me search for other places that match on `PropertyKey`:

```ts

```

In this case, `"test-a"` is a string literal key (non-computed), but the value `sideEffect()` has side effects. My code tries to substitute `o` in `sideEffect()`, which doesn't contain `o`, so it returns `None`. Then it continues to the next property `testb: o` and successfully inlines `o`. Is this correct?

The original code for `StaticIdentifier` keys would do the same thing: try to substitute in the value, fail, then continue to the next property. So this behavior is consistent.

There\'s also an unrelated snapshot change in `stacktrace_is_correct.snap` (Node.js version change), but that\'s not related to my changes.\n\nLet me summarize the fix:\n\n## Summary\n\nThe bug was in the `substitute_single_use_symbol_in_expression` function in `/testbed/crates/oxc_minifier/src/peephole/minimize_statements.rs`. \n\nWhen processing object expressions to inline variables, the code iterates over object properties. For each property, it checks if the variable to inline is used in the property\'s key or value. \n\nThe original code had two branches for property keys:\n1. `PropertyKey::StaticIdentifier` / `PropertyKey::PrivateIdentifier` - These are simple identifiers like `testb` in `{ testb: o }`. The code would try to substitute in the value, and if not found, continue to the next property.\n2. All other expression-based keys (via `match_expression!(PropertyKey)`) - This includes `StringLiteral` keys like `"test-a"` in `{ "test-a": "test-a" }`. The code would try to substitute in the key expression, and then **unconditionally return `Some(false)`**, which prevented looking at any subsequent properties.\n\nThe comment said "Stop now because computed keys have side effects", but the code wasn\'t actually checking whether the key was computed - it was treating ALL expression-based keys as computed, even non-computed string literals like `"test-a"`.\n\n**The fix:** \n- First check if the property key is non-computed (`!prop.computed`). If so, treat it like `StaticIdentifier` keys: try to substitute in the value, and if the variable isn\'t found, continue to the next property (using `continue`).\n- Only for computed keys (`prop.computed == true`), apply the original logic: try the key expression, then return `Some(false)` if not found (since computed keys may have side effects).\n\nThis correctly handles the case where a non-computed string literal key (like `"test-a"`) appears before the property that uses the variable to be inlined (like `testb: o`).</think>The issue was a bug in the minifier\'s variable inlining logic where string keys in object literals (like `"test-a"`) would prevent inlining of variables used in subsequent properties. The problem occurred in the `substitute_single_use_symbol_in_expression` function when processing `ObjectExpression` nodes.\n\n### Root Cause:\nWhen iterating over object properties looking for a variable to inline, the code would encounter non-computed string literal keys (e.g., `"test-a": "test-a"`) and mistakenly treat them as computed keys, causing it to return `Some(false)` and stop searching immediately. This prevented it from finding the variable in later properties (e.g., `testb: o`).\n\n### Changes Made:\n\n1. **Fixed `crates/oxc_minifier/src/peephole/minimize_statements.rs` - `substitute_single_use_symbol_in_expression` function**:\n   - Added a check for `!prop.computed` to handle non-computed keys (including string literals) the same way as `StaticIdentifier` keys\n   - For non-computed keys: try substitution in the value, and if not found, continue to the next property\n   - For computed keys: keep the original logic (check key expression first, then stop with `Some(false)`)\n   - This allows the function to skip over non-computed string literal keys and continue searching for the variable in subsequent properties\n\n### Key Features:\n- ✅ Variables are now properly inlined when string literal keys appear before them in object literals\n- ✅ Non-computed string literal keys are treated like `StaticIdentifier` keys (no side effects)\n- ✅ Computed keys still correctly stop the search (they have side effects)\n- ✅ `__proto__` shorthand handling is preserved for both computed and non-computed keys\n- ✅ All existing tests continue to pass\n- ✅ The fix is minimal and doesn\'t affect other optimization paths\n\nThe fix ensures that the minifier correctly inlines variables in object literals even when string literal keys are present, matching the expected behavior shown in the PR description.', role='assistant', tool_calls=None, function_call=None, provider_specific_fields={'refusal': None}), provider_specific_fields={'content_filter_results': {}})], usage=Usage(completion_tokens=906, prompt_tokens=127570, total_tokens=128476, completion_tokens_details=None, prompt_tokens_details=None, audio_prompt_tokens=0), service_tier=None, prompt_filter_results=None)
